NOTE 14 &#x2013; INCOME TAXES




The Company files income tax returns in the U.S. Federal
jurisdiction and various state jurisdictions.



Income taxes are accounted for under the asset and liability
method. Deferred tax assets and liabilities are recognized for the
future tax consequences attributable to differences between the
financial statement carrying amounts of existing assets and
liabilities and their respective tax bases and operating loss and
tax credit carryforwards. Deferred tax assets and liabilities are
measured using enacted tax rates expected to apply to taxable
income in the years in which those temporary differences are
expected to be recovered or settled. The Company must assess the
likelihood that its deferred tax assets will be recovered from
future taxable income and
 to the extent that it is more likely
than not that such deferred tax assets will not be realized
 the
Company must establish a valuation allowance.



As of December 31
 2017 and 2016
 the Company has a valuation
allowance against 100% of the deferred tax assets
 which is
)
carryforwards. Even though the Company has reserved all of these
net deferred tax assets for book purposes
 the Company would still
be able to utilize them to reduce future income taxes payable
should the Company have future taxable earnings. To the extent the
deferred tax assets relate to NOL carryforwards
 the ability to use
such NOLs against future earnings will be subject to applicable
carryforward periods. As of December 31
 2017 and 2016
 the Company
had NOL carryforwards for both Federal and state tax purposes of
approximately $

 which are available to offset
. Our NOL carryforwards begin to expire in
2028.



In December 2017
 the Tax Cuts and Jobs Act (the &#x201C;2017 Tax
Act&#x201D;) was enacted. The 2017 Tax Act includes a number of
changes to existing U.S. tax laws that impact the Company
 most
notably a reduction of the U.S. corporate income tax rate from 35
percent to 21 percent for tax years beginning after December 31
2017. The 2017 Tax Act also provides for a one-time transition tax
on certain foreign earnings and the acceleration of depreciation
for certain assets placed into service after September 27
 2017 as
well as prospective changes beginning in 2018
 including changing
rules related to uses and limitations of net operating loss
carryforwards created in tax years beginning after December 31
2017. Specifically
 the 2017 Tax Act limits the amount the Company
is able to deduct for net operating loss carryforwards generated in
taxable years beginning after December 31
 2017 to 80% of taxable
income however these net operating loss carryforwards can be
carried forward indefinitely
 repeal of the domestic manufacturing
deduction
 acceleration of tax revenue recognition
 capitalization
of research and development expenditures
 additional limitations on
executive compensation and limitations on the deductibility of
interest.



The changes to existing U.S. tax laws as a result of the 2017 Tax
Act
 which the Company believes has the most significant impact on
the Company&#x2019;s federal income taxes are as
follows:



Reduction of the U.S. Corporate Income Tax Rate



The Company measures deferred tax assets and liabilities using
enacted tax rates that will apply in the years in which the
temporary differences are expected to be recovered or paid.
Accordingly
 the Company&#x2019;s deferred tax assets and
liabilities were remeasured to reflect the reduction in the U.S.
corporate income tax rate from 35 percent to 21 percent
 resulting
million decrease in net deferred tax assets and a
million decrease in the valuation allowance as of
December 31
 2017.

ITEM 9A. CONTROLS AND PROCEDURES




Disclosure Controls and Procedures




Company maintains disclosure controls and procedures that are
designed to ensure that information required to be disclosed in our
reports filed under the Exchange Act
 is recorded
 processed
summarized and reported within the time periods specified in the
SEC&#x2019;s rules and forms
 and that such information is
accumulated and communicated to our management
 including our chief
executive officer (and our chief financial officer
 as appropriate
to allow for timely decisions regarding required disclosure. In
designing and evaluating our disclosure controls and procedures
management recognizes that any controls and procedures
 no matter
how well designed and operated
 can provide only reasonable
assurance of achieving the desired control objectives
 and
management is required to apply its judgment in evaluating the
cost&#xAD;benefit relationship of possible controls and procedures.
Our management
 with the participation of our principal executive
officer and chief financial officer (our principal financial
officer)
 has evaluated the effectiveness of our disclosure
controls and procedures (as defined in Exchange Act Rules
131&#xAD;15(e) and 15d&#xAD;15(e)) as of December 31
 2017. Based
on that evaluation
 our management concluded that our disclosure
controls and procedures were effective as of December 31
2017.



















Management&#x2019;s Report on Internal Control Over Financial
Reporting


&#xA0;


is responsible for establishing and maintaining adequate internal
control over the Company&#x2019;s financial reporting. In order to
evaluate the effectiveness of internal control over financial
reporting
 as required by Section 404 of the Sarbanes-Oxley Act of
2002
 our management
 with the participation of our principal
executive officer and principal financial officer has conducted an
assessment
 including testing
 using the criteria in Internal
Control &#x2013; Integrated Framework
 issued by the Committee of
Sponsoring Organizations of the Treadway Commission
&#x201D;)
(2013). Our system of internal control over financial reporting is
designed to provide reasonable assurance regarding the reliability
of financial reporting and the preparation of financial statements
for external purposes in accordance with generally accepted
accounting principles. Because of its inherent limitations
internal control over financial reporting may not prevent or detect
misstatements. This assessment included review of the documentation
of controls
 evaluation of the design effectiveness of controls
testing of the operating effectiveness of controls and a conclusion
on this evaluation.




Based on this evaluation
 management concluded that our internal
control over financial reporting was effective as of December 31
2017 and 2016. 



&#xA0;


currently reviewing our disclosure controls and procedures related
to all risk areas and expect to continually improve in the next
calendar year
 including identifying specific areas within our
governance
 accounting and financial reporting processes to add
adequate resources to mitigate any potential
weaknesses.




management will continue to monitor and evaluate the effectiveness
of our internal controls and procedures and our internal controls
over financial reporting on an ongoing basis and is committed to
taking further action and implementing additional enhancements or
improvements
 as necessary and as funds allow.




of its inherent limitations
 internal controls over financial
reporting may not prevent or detect misstatements. Projections of
any evaluation of effectiveness to future periods are subject to
the risk that controls may become inadequate because of changes in
conditions
 or that the degree of compliance with the policies or
procedures may deteriorate. All internal control systems
 no matter
how well designed
 have inherent limitations. Therefore
 even those
systems determined to be effective can provide only reasonable
assurance with respect to financial statement preparation and
presentation.




Changes in Internal Control Over Financial Reporting




were no changes in our internal control over financial reporting
during the years ended December 31
 2017 and 2016 that have
materially affected
 or are reasonably likely to materially affect
our internal control over financial reporting. We believe that a
control system
 no matter how well designed and operated
 cannot
provide absolute assurance that the objectives of the control
system are met
 and no evaluation of controls can provide absolute
assurance that all control issues and instances of fraud
 if any
within any company have been detected.

Neil Fallon &#x2013; Executive Chairman




Fallon has been a Director of the Company since inception on April
26
 2010
 and served as Chief Executive Officer and Chief Financial
Officer from inception until March 24
 2016. Mr. Fallon previously
owned his own residential real estate development company
 Neil
Fallon Development

sites through California and Washington states from May 2002 to
July 2015. He specialized in the development of infill properties
averaging in the range of 30&#xAD;50 home sites. Mr. Fallon has a
BA in Business Administration with concentrations in Finance and
Marketing from Western Washington University.




Fallon was chosen to serve as a director of the company due to the
fact that he is the founder of the company and possesses valuable
business experience related to acting in a management
role.

 Director

 tea
 and other healthy segments.


&#xA0;


Corporate Governance




board of directors maintains an audit committee
 compensation
committee and nominating and corporate governance committee. Each
committee operates under a charter approved by our board of
directors in connection. Copies of each charter are posted in the

www.newagebev.com.




Audit Committee




functions of the Audit Committee are to (i) review the
qualifications of the independent auditors
 our annual and interim
financial statements
 the independent auditor&#x2019;s report
significant reporting or operating issues and corporate policies
and procedures as they relate to accounting and financial controls;
and (ii) to consider and review other matters relating to our
financial and accounting affairs. Mr. Vautrin
 Dr. Kapteyn and Mr.
Fea serve as members of the Company&#x2019;s audit committee
 with
Mr. Vautrin acting as the audit committee chairman and financial
expert.



















Compensation Committee




function of the Compensation Committee is to discharge the
Board&#x2019;s responsibilities relating to compensation of the
Company&#x2019;s directors and executive officers
 to produce an
annual report on executive compensation for inclusion in the
Company&#x2019;s annual proxy statement
 as necessary
 and to
oversee and advise the Board on the adoption of policies that
govern the Company&#x2019;s compensation programs including stock
incentive and benefit plans. Mr. Vautrin
 Mr. Brennan
 and Dr.
Kapteyn serve as members of the Company&#x2019;s compensation
committee
 with Mr. Fea serving as the compensation committee
chairman.




Nominating and Governance Committee




The function of the Nominating and Governance Committee is to (i)
make recommendations to the Board regarding the size of the Board
(ii) make recommendations to the Board regarding criteria for the
selection of director nominees
 (iii) identify and recommend to the
Board for selection as director nominees individuals qualified to
become members of the Board
 (iv) recommend committee assignments
to the Board
 (v) recommend to the Board corporate governance
principles and practices appropriate to the Company
 and (vi) lead
the Board in an annual review of its performance. Mr. Fea and Mr.
Haas serve as members of the Company&#x2019;s governance committee
with Mr. Haas serving as the governance committee
chairman.




Director Independence




Company is quoted on The NASDAQ Capital Market which requires that
a majority of the board of directors must be comprised of
&#x201C;independent&#x201D; directors as such term is defined in Rule
5605(a)(2). For purposes of determining director independence
 we
have applied the definitions set forth in The NASDAQ Capital Market
guidelines which state
 generally
 that a director is not
considered to be independent if he or she is
 or at any time during
the past three years was an employee of the Company or if he or she
(or his or her family member) accepted compensation from the
Company in excess of $120
000 during any twelve month period within
the three years preceding the determination of independence
 among
others. Our Board has affirmatively determined that Mr. Vautrin
Dr. Kapteyn
 Mr. Brennan
 Mr. Haas and Mr. Fea are
&#x201C;independent&#x201D; directors as such term is defined under
The NASDAQ Capital Market rules and the related rules of the
SEC.




Board Meetings; Committee Meetings; and Annual Meeting
Attendance



the year ended 2017
 the Board of Directors held four meetings. The
Audit Committee met four times. The Compensation Committee met four
times. The Nominating and Governance Committee met four times. We
do not have a formal policy in place with respect to director
attendance at the Company&#x2019;s annual meeting of
shareholders.




Board Leadership Structure




Board has no set policy with respect to the separation of the
offices of Executive Chairman and Chief Executive Officer.
Currently
 Neil Fallon serves as Executive Chairman and Brent
Willis serves as Chief Executive Officer. Our board of directors
does not have a lead independent director. Our board of directors
has determined that its leadership structure is appropriate and
effective for us at this time
 given our stage of
development.




Board of Director&#x2019;s Role in Risk Oversight




Board is responsible for overseeing our management and operations
including overseeing our risk assessment and risk management
functions. We believe that our directors provide effective
oversight of risk management functions. On a regular basis we
perform a risk review wherein the management team evaluates the
risks we expect to face in the upcoming year and over a longer term
horizon. From this risk assessment plans are developed to deal with
the risks identified. The results of this risk assessment are
provided to the Board for their consideration and review. In
addition
 members of our management periodically present to the
Board the strategies
 issues and plans for the areas of our
business for which they are responsible. While the Board oversees
risk management
 our management is responsible for day-to-day risk
management processes. Additionally
 the Board requires that
management raise exceptional issues to the Board. We believe this
division of responsibilities is the most effective approach for
addressing the risks we face and that the Board leadership
structure supports this approach.




Code of Business Conduct and Ethics




adopted a Code of Business Conduct and Ethics that applies to our
principal executive
 financial and accounting officers (or persons
performing similar functions)
a copy of which is filed as Exhibit
14.1 to this Annual Report.




Family Relationships



There are no family relationships among the officers and directors
nor are there any arrangements or understanding between any of the
Directors or Officers of our Company or any other person pursuant
to which any Officer or Director was or is to be selected as an
officer or director.



16(a) Beneficial Ownership Reporting Compliance




on a review of reports filed by our directors
 executive officers
and beneficial owners of more than 10% of our shares of common

1934
 as amended
 and other information available to us
 we believe
that all such ownership reports required to be filed by those
reporting persons during and with respect to Fiscal 2017 were
timely made.





Involvement in Certain Legal Proceedings



During the last ten years
 none of our officers
 directors
promoters or control persons have been involved in any legal
proceedings as described in Item 401(f) of Regulation
S-K.

New Age Beverages Code of Ethics and Conduct




Beverages Corporation is committed to conducting our business in
accordance with applicable laws
 rules
 and regulations and the
highest standards of business ethics. This Code of Business Ethics
and Conduct reflects the business practices and principles of
behavior that support this commitment. We expect every officer
director
 and associate of the Company
 its subsidiaries and
affiliates to read and understand the Code of Ethics and abide by
it in the performance of his/her business responsibilities. The
Code of Ethics is designed to represent key guiding principles for
the Company&#x2019;s officers
 directors
 and associates and should
not be understood to replace or eliminate any additional
obligations set forth in applicable Company personnel policies or
agreements.




Code of Ethics does not cover every issue that may arise. If you
have any questions about the proper course of conduct in any
situation
 you should seek assistance from your manager
 the
Company&#x2019;s legal counsel or other Company
resources.




extent that a law conflicts with a policy in this Code of Ethics
you must comply with the law; however
 if a local custom or policy
conflicts with this Code of Ethics
 you must comply with the Code
of Ethics.




Company associate must abide by our Code of Ethics. Adherence to
the Code of Ethics is a condition to employment and is not optional


don&#x2019;t live our values are subject to disciplinary action
 up
to and including termination of employment. Violations of the Code
of Ethics by agents of the Company might also result in
disciplinary action against those officers
 directors or associates
with responsibility and oversight of those agents. Violations of
this Code of Ethics may also mean that you or the Company&#x2019;s
agents are breaking the law
 subjecting you (and possibly the
Company) to criminal or civil sanctions or penalties
 including
monetary fines and/or prison.

&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;On April 1, 2015, American Brewing acquired&#13;the assets of B&amp;#38;R Liquid Adventure, which included the brand, B&amp;#250;cha Live Kombucha. Prior to acquiring the B&amp;#250;cha Live&#13;Kombucha brand and business, we were a craft brewery operation. In April 2016, new management assumed daily operation of the business,&#13;and began the implementation of a new vision for the Company. In May 2016 we changed our name to B&amp;#250;cha, Inc. (&amp;#8220;B&amp;#250;cha&amp;#8221;),&#13;and then on June 30, 2016, we acquired the combined assets of &amp;#8220;Xing&amp;#8221; including Xing Beverage, LLC, New Age Beverages,&#13;LLC, Aspen Pure, LLC, and New Age Properties. We then shut down all California operations where B&amp;#250;cha was based, relocated&#13;the Company&amp;#8217;s operational headquarters to Denver, Colorado, and changed our name to New Age Beverages Corporation. On October&#13;1, 2016, we then sold American Brewing including their brewery, brewery assets and its related liabilities to focus exclusively&#13;on the healthy beverages. We recognized the sale of our brewery and brewery operations as a discontinued operation beginning in&#13;the third quarter of 2016, and ultimately concluded the transaction in February 2017. In February 2017, we uplisted onto The NASDAQ&#13;Capital Market. In March 2017, we acquired the assets of Maverick Brands, including their brand Coco-Libre. In June 2017, we acquired&#13;the assets of Premier Micronutrient Corporation (&amp;#8220;PMC&amp;#8221;), and also completed the acquisition of the Marley Beverage&#13;Company (&amp;#8220;Marley&amp;#8221;) including the brand licensing rights to all Marley brand ready to drink beverages.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&lt;b&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;We have three wholly-owned subsidiaries, NABC,&#13;Inc., NABC Properties, LLC (&amp;#8220;NABC Properties&amp;#8221;), and New Age Health Sciences. NABC, Inc. is our Colorado-based operating company&#13;that consolidates performance and financial results of our divisions. NABC Properties incorporates all our buildings and warehouses,&#13;and New Age Health Sciences includes all our patents, and the operating performance in the medical and hospital channels.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&lt;b&gt;&lt;i&gt;Reclassification &lt;/i&gt;&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&lt;b&gt;&lt;i&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;Certain amounts in the prior periods presented&#13;have been reclassified to conform to the current period financial statement presentation. These reclassifications have no effect&#13;on previously reported net income.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&lt;b&gt;&lt;i&gt;Basis of Presentation&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;The accompanying audited consolidated financial&#13;statements and related footnotes have been prepared in accordance with accounting principles generally accepted in the United States&#13;of America (or U.S. GAAP) and with the Securities and Exchange Commission&amp;#8217;s (or SEC) instructions for the Form 10-K.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&lt;b&gt;&lt;i&gt;Principles of Consolidation&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;Our consolidated financial statements include&#13;the accounts of all majority-owned subsidiary companies. All intercompany transactions and balances have been eliminated.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&lt;b&gt;&lt;i&gt;Use of Estimates&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;The preparation of the consolidated financial&#13;statements in conformity with U.S. GAAP requires management to make estimates and assumptions that affect the reported amounts&#13;of assets and liabilities and disclosure of contingent assets and liabilities at the date of the consolidated financial statements&#13;and the reported amounts of revenue and expenses during the reporting period. Actual results could differ from those estimates.&#13;The more significant estimates and assumptions made by management include allowance for doubtful accounts, inventory valuation,&#13;provision for excess or expired inventory, depreciation of property and equipment, realizability of long-lived assets, allowance&#13;for sales returns and chargebacks, estimated cash flows in the acquisitions, and fair market value of equity instruments issued&#13;for goods or services. The current economic environment has increased the degree and uncertainty inherent in these estimates and&#13;assumptions.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&lt;b&gt;&lt;i&gt;Cash and Cash Equivalents&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; color: #231F20&gt;Cash and cash equivalents as&#13;of December 31, 2017 and 2016 included cash on-hand. Cash equivalents are considered all accounts with an original maturity date&#13;within 90 days.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&lt;b&gt;&lt;i&gt;Accounts Receivable&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/b&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;The Company&amp;#8217;s accounts receivable&#13;primarily consists of trade receivables. The Company records an allowance for doubtful accounts that is based on historical&#13;trends, customer knowledge, any known disputes, and the aging of the accounts receivable balances combined with&#13;management&amp;#8217;s estimate of future potential recoverability. Receivables are written off against the allowance after all&#13;attempts to collect a receivable have failed. The Company&amp;#8217;s allowance for doubtful accounts was $52,345 as of December&#13;31, 2017 and $46,350 as of December 31, 2016.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&lt;b&gt;&lt;i&gt;Concentrations of Credit Risk&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;Financial instruments that potentially subject&#13;the Company to concentrations of credit risk consist principally of cash and accounts receivables.&amp;#160; The Company places its&#13;cash with high credit quality financial institutions.&amp;#160; At times such amounts may exceed federally insured limits.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;For the year ended December 31, 2017, three&#13;customers represented approximately 21.4% (9.9%, 6.3% and 5.2%) of net revenues. For the year ended December 31, 2016, three customers&#13;represented approximately 27.5% (14.5%, 7.5% and 5.5%) of net revenues. As of December 31, 2017, three customers represented 23.1%&#13;(10.5%, 6.7% and 5.9%) of accounts receivables. As of December 31, 2016, three customers represented approximately 29.4% (12.3%,&#13;8.9% and 8.2%) of accounts receivable.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&lt;b&gt;&lt;i&gt;Fair Value of Financial Instruments&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&lt;b&gt;&lt;i&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;The carrying amount of the financial instruments,&#13;which principally include cash, trade receivables, accounts payable and accrued expenses, approximates fair value due to the relative&#13;short maturity of such instruments. The carrying amount of the Company&amp;#8217;s debt approximates its fair value as it bears interest&#13;at market rates of interest after taking into consideration the debt discounts.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 27pt&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;Accounting Standards Codification (ASC) 820&#13;defines fair value, establishes a framework for measuring fair value under U.S. GAAP and enhances disclosures about fair value&#13;measurements. Fair value is defined under ASC 820 as the exchange price that would be received for an asset or paid to transfer&#13;a liability (an exit price) in the principal or most advantageous market for the asset or liability in an orderly transaction between&#13;market participants on the measurement date. Valuation techniques used to measure fair value under ASC 820 must maximize the use&#13;of observable inputs and minimize the use of unobservable inputs. The standard describes a fair-value hierarchy based on three&#13;levels of inputs, of which the first two are considered observable and the last unobservable, that may be used to measure fair&#13;value as follows:&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 27pt&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 27pt&gt;&lt;b&gt;&lt;i&gt;Level 1&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/b&gt;&amp;#8212;Quoted&#13;prices in active markets for identical assets or liabilities.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 27pt&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 27pt&gt;&lt;b&gt;&lt;i&gt;Level 2&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/b&gt;&amp;#8212;Inputs&#13;other than Level 1 that are observable, either directly or indirectly, such as quoted prices for similar assets or liabilities;&#13;quoted prices in markets that are not active; or other inputs that are observable or can be corroborated by observable market data&#13;for substantially the full term of the assets or liabilities.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 27pt&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 27pt&gt;&lt;b&gt;&lt;i&gt;Level 3&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/b&gt;&amp;#8212;Unobservable&#13;inputs that are supported by little or no market activity and that are significant to the fair value of the assets or liabilities.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 27pt&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 10pt 0 0; text-indent: 24.5pt&gt;The following tables set forth the fair&#13;value of the Company&amp;#8217;s contingent provision as of December&amp;#160;31, 2017 and 2016:&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0&gt;&lt;font style=font: 8pt Times New Roman

 Serif&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=margin: 0&gt;&lt;font style=font: 8pt Times New Roman

 Serif&gt;There were no transfers between&#13;levels within the fair value hierarchy during the periods presented.&amp;#160;&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&lt;b&gt;&lt;i&gt;Goodwill and Customer Relationships&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; color: #231F20&gt;Goodwill represents the excess&#13;of the purchase price of acquired businesses over the estimated fair value of the identifiable net assets acquired. Goodwill and&#13;other intangibles with indefinite useful lives are not amortized but tested for impairment annually or more frequently when events&#13;or circumstances indicates that the carrying value of a reporting unit more likely than not exceeds its fair value. The goodwill&#13;impairment test is applied by performing a qualitative assessment before calculating the fair value of the reporting unit. If,&#13;on the basis of qualitative factors, it is considered not more likely than not that the fair value of the reporting unit is less&#13;than the carrying amount, further testing of goodwill for impairment would not be required. If the carrying amount of a reporting&#13;unit exceeds the reporting unit&amp;#8217;s fair value, an impairment loss is recognized in an amount equal to that excess, limited&#13;to the total amount of goodwill allocated to that reporting unit. The Company performed a qualitative assessment and determined&#13;there was no impairment of goodwill for the years ended December 31, 2017 and 2016.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;Intangible assets are recorded at acquisition&#13;fair value as part of the acquisitions. The balance as of December 31, 2017 and 2016 is reflected net of accumulated amortization.&#13;Definite lived intangible assets are amortized over their estimated useful life using the straight-line method, which is determined&#13;by identifying the period over which the cash flows from the asset are expected to be generated, typically 15 to 42 years. As of&#13;December 31, 2017 and 2016 accumulated amortization was $1,368,568 and $340,126, respectively. Amortization expense was $1,028,443&#13;and $340,126 for the years ended December 31, 2017 and 2016, respectively.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&lt;i&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&lt;b&gt;&lt;i&gt;Long-lived Assets&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;Long-lived assets consisted of property and&#13;equipment and customer relationships and are reviewed for impairment in accordance with the guidance of the ASC 360, Property,&#13;Plant, and Equipment. The Company tests for impairment losses on long-lived assets used in operations whenever events or changes&#13;in circumstances indicate that the carrying amount of the asset may not be recoverable. For the years ended December 31, 2017 and&#13;2016, respectively, the Company had not experienced impairment losses on the long-lived assets as management determined that there&#13;were no indicators that the carrying amount of the asset may not be recoverable.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&lt;b&gt;&lt;i&gt;Share-Based Compensation&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;The Company accounts for share-based&#13;compensation to employees in accordance with ASC 718 &lt;i&gt;Compensation&amp;#8212;Stock Compensation. Share &lt;/i&gt;based compensation&#13;to employees is measured at the grant date, based on the fair value of the award, and is recognized as expense over the&#13;requisite employee service period. The Company accounts for share based compensation to other than employees in accordance&#13;with Financial Standards Accounting Board (FASB) ASC 505-50. Equity instruments issued to other than employees are valued at&#13;the earlier of a commitment date or upon completion of the services, based on the fair value of the equity instruments and is&#13;recognized as expense over the service period. The Company estimates the fair value of share based payments using the&#13;Black-Scholes option pricing model for common stock options and warrants and the latest fair market price of the&#13;Company&amp;#8217;s common stock for common share issuances. The Company has not experienced any forfeitures and does not expect&#13;forfeitures.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;Included in prepaid expenses as of December&#13;31, 2017 and 2016 are prepaid share-based compensation of approximately $1,000,000 and $-, of which approximately $500,000 and&#13;$- are presented as long-term on the consolidated balance sheets under the caption Prepaid Expenses, long-term. These amounts represent&#13;the prepaid compensation to employees and certain non-employees for services rendered.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&lt;b&gt;&lt;i&gt;Inventories and Provision for Excess or&#13;Expired Inventory&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;Inventories consist of tea ingredients, packaging&#13;and finished goods and are stated at the lower of cost (first-in, first-out basis) or market value.&amp;#160; Provisions for excess&#13;inventory are included in cost of goods sold and have historically been immaterial but adequate to provide for losses on its raw&#13;materials.&amp;#160; There was no reserve for obsolescence as of December 31, 2017 and December 31, 2016.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&lt;b&gt;&lt;i&gt;Property and Equipment&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;Property and equipment consists primarily of&#13;brewing equipment and are stated at cost.&amp;#160; Depreciation is computed using the straight-line method based upon the estimated&#13;useful lives of the underlying assets, generally five years.&amp;#160; Major renewals and betterments that extend the life of the property&#13;are capitalized.&amp;#160; Expenditures for repairs and maintenance are expensed as incurred.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&lt;b&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&lt;b&gt;&lt;i&gt;Revenue Recognition&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;The Company&amp;#8217;s products are distributed&#13;in major health and grocery chains throughout North America.&amp;#160; Revenue is recognized upon delivery of goods to the customer.&amp;#160;&#13;An allowance for estimated returns is provided at the time of the sale.&amp;#160; In accordance with the guidance in FASB Topic ASC&#13;605, &lt;i&gt;Revenue Recognition&lt;/i&gt;, the Company recognizes revenue when (a) persuasive evidence of an arrangement exists, (b) delivery&#13;has occurred or services have been rendered, (c) the fee is fixed or determinable, and (d) collectability is reasonable assured.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&lt;b&gt;&lt;i&gt;&amp;#160;&amp;#160;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&lt;b&gt;&lt;i&gt;Customer Programs and Incentives&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;Customer programs and incentives, which include&#13;customer promotional discount programs and customer incentives, are a common practice in the beverage industry.&amp;#160; The Company&#13;incurs customer program costs to promote sales of products and to maintain competitive pricing.&amp;#160; Amounts paid in connection&#13;with customer programs and incentives are recorded as reductions to net revenue or as advertising, promotional and selling expenses&#13;in accordance with ASC Topic 605-50, &lt;i&gt;Revenue Recognition&amp;#8212;Customer Payments and Incentives&lt;/i&gt;, based on the nature of&#13;the expenditure.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&lt;b&gt;&lt;i&gt;Cost of Goods Sold&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;Cost of goods sold mainly consisted of raw material&#13;costs, packaging costs and direct labor.&amp;#160; Costs are recognized when the related revenue is recorded.&amp;#160; Shipping and handling&#13;costs for all wholesale sales transactions are billed to the customer and are included in costs of goods sold for all periods presented.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0&gt;&lt;b&gt;&lt;i&gt;Advertising, Promotions and Sales&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;Advertising, promotional and selling expenses&#13;consisted of sales salaries, tap handles, media advertising costs, sales and marketing expenses, and promotional activity expenses&#13;and are recognized when incurred in the accompanying consolidated statements of operations.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&lt;b&gt;&lt;i&gt;General and Administrative Expenses&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;General and administrative expenses consisted&#13;of professional service fees, rent and utility expenses, meals, travel and entertainment expenses, and other general and administrative&#13;overhead costs.&amp;#160; Expenses are recognized when incurred.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&lt;b&gt;&lt;i&gt;Income Taxes&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 27pt&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;The Company accounts for income taxes pursuant&#13;to the provisions of ASC 740, &lt;i&gt;Income Taxes&lt;/i&gt;, whereby deferred tax assets and liabilities are recognized for the future tax&#13;consequences attributable to differences between the financial statement carrying amount of existing assets and liabilities and&#13;their respective tax bases and the future tax benefits derived from operating loss and tax credit carryforwards. The Company provides&#13;a valuation allowance on our deferred tax assets when it is more likely than not that such deferred tax assets will not be realized.&#13;The Company has a valuation allowance against 100% of the net deferred tax assets.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 27pt&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;ASC 740 requires that the Company recognize&#13;in the consolidated financial statements the effect of a tax position that is more likely than not to be sustained upon examination&#13;based on the technical merits of the position. The first step is to determine whether or not a tax benefit should be recognized.&#13;A tax benefit will be recognized if the weight of available evidence indicates that the tax position is more likely than not to&#13;be sustained upon examination by the relevant tax authorities. The recognition and measurement of benefits related to our tax positions&#13;requires significant judgment as uncertainties often exist with respect to new laws, new interpretations of existing laws, and&#13;rulings by taxing authorities. Differences between actual results and our assumptions, or changes in our assumptions in future&#13;periods, are recorded in the period they become known. For tax liabilities, the Company recognizes accrued interest related to&#13;uncertain tax positions as a component of income tax expense, and penalties, if incurred, are recognized as a component of operating&#13;expense.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&lt;b&gt;&lt;i&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&lt;b&gt;&lt;i&gt;Net Income (Loss) Per Share&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;Basic net income (loss) per share is calculated&#13;by dividing net income (loss) by the weighted-average common shares outstanding.&amp;#160; Diluted net income per share is calculated&#13;by dividing net income by the weighted-average common shares outstanding during the period using the treasury stock method or the&#13;two-class method, whichever is more dilutive.&amp;#160; As the Company incurred net losses for the periods ended December 31, 2017&#13;and 2016 no potentially dilutive securities were included in the calculation of diluted earnings per share as the impact would&#13;have been anti-dilutive.&amp;#160; Therefore, basic and dilutive net income (loss) per share were the same.&amp;#160; If the Company had&#13;net income, potential dilutive securities consist of warrants to purchase zero and 1,127,000 shares of common stock as of December&#13;31, 2017 and December 31, 2016, respectively.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&lt;b&gt;&lt;i&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&lt;b&gt;&lt;i&gt;Recently Issued Accounting Standards&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 27pt&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;In May 2014, the FASB issued ASU No. 2014-09,&#13;Revenue from Contracts with Customers, as a new Topic, ASC Topic 606.&amp;#160;The new revenue recognition standard provides a five-step&#13;analysis of transactions to determine when and how revenue is recognized.&amp;#160;The core principle is that a company should recognize&#13;revenue to depict the transfer of promised goods or services to customers in an amount that reflects the consideration to which&#13;the entity expects to be entitled in exchange for those goods or services. In August 2015, the FASB issued ASU No. 2015-14, Revenue&#13;from Contracts with Customers: Deferral of the Effective Date, which deferred the effective date of the new revenue standard for&#13;periods beginning after December 15, 2016 to December 15, 2017, with early adoption permitted but not earlier than the original&#13;effective date. This ASU must be applied retrospectively to each period presented or as a cumulative-effect adjustment as of the&#13;date of adoption.&amp;#160;The Company is considering the alternatives of adoption of this ASU and is conducting its review of the&#13;likely impact to the existing portfolio of customer contracts entered into prior to adoption. After completing its review, the&#13;Company will continue to evaluate the effect of adopting this guidance upon the Company results of operations, cash flows and financial&#13;position. Currently, the Company does not expect the adoption of this ASU to have a material impact on its financial statements&#13;except that there are significant additional reporting requirements under the new standard.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;In February 2016, the FASB issued ASU No. 2016-02,&#13;Leases. This ASU establishes a right-of-use (ROU) model that requires a lessee to record a ROU asset and a lease liability on the&#13;balance sheet for all leases with terms longer than 12 months. Leases will be classified as either finance or operating, with classification&#13;affecting the pattern of expense recognition in the income statement. This ASU is effective for fiscal years beginning after December&#13;15, 2018, including interim periods within those fiscal years. A modified retrospective transition approach is required for lessees&#13;for capital and operating leases existing at, or entered into after, the beginning of the earliest comparative period presented&#13;in the financial statements, with certain practical expedients available. During the year ended December 31, 2017 management elected&#13;to early adopt the guidance under ASU 2016-02. Management&amp;#8217;s decision was based on the stock price during the year would most&#13;likely result in the Company entering into and being designated an accelerated filer by June 30, 2019, which would result in management&#13;having to restate the financial statements to reflect the adoption of the new standard.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 27pt&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;In March 2016, the FASB issued ASU 2016-08,&#13;Revenue from Contracts with Customers (Topic 606). This ASU is related to reporting revenue gross versus net, or principal versus&#13;agent considerations. This ASU is meant to clarify the guidance in ASU 2014-09,&amp;#160;Revenue from Contracts with Customers, as&#13;it pertains to principal versus agent considerations. Specifically, the guidance addresses how entities should identify goods and&#13;services being provided to a customer, the unit of account for a principal versus agent assessment, how to evaluate whether a good&#13;or service is controlled before being transferred to a customer, and how to assess whether an entity controls services performed&#13;by another party. This ASU has the same effective date as the new revenue standard, which is effective for fiscal years, and for&#13;interim periods within those fiscal years, beginning after December 15, 2017. The Company is evaluating the effect and methodology&#13;of adopting this new accounting guidance upon the Company results of operations, cash flows and financial position. The Company&#13;has begun to consider the alternatives of adoption of this ASU, and has started its review of the likely impact to the existing&#13;portfolio of customer contracts entered into prior to adoption. The Company will also continue to evaluate the effect of adopting&#13;this guidance upon its results of operations, cash flows and financial position. Currently, the Company does not expect the adoption&#13;of this ASU to have a material impact on its consolidated financial statements except that there are significant additional reporting&#13;requirements under the new standard.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: center&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;In March 2016, the FASB issued ASU&#13;2016-09, Compensation-Stock Compensation (Topic 718). This ASU is related to simplifications of employee share-based payment&#13;accounting. This pronouncement eliminates the APIC pool concept and requires that excess tax benefits and tax deficiencies be&#13;recorded in the income statement when awards are settled. The pronouncement also addresses simplifications related to&#13;statement of cash flows classification, accounting for forfeitures and minimum statutory tax withholding requirements. This&#13;ASU is effective for fiscal years, and for interim periods within those fiscal years, beginning after December 15, 2016.&#13;    This ASU does  not have a material impact on the Company&amp;#8217;s consolidated financial&#13;statements based on managements conclusion.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;In April 2016, the FASB issued ASU 2016-10,&#13;Revenue from Contracts with Customers (Topic 606): Identifying Performance Obligations and Licensing. This ASU is meant to clarify&#13;the guidance in FASB ASU 2014-09,&amp;#160;Revenue from Contracts with Customers. Specifically, the guidance addresses an entity&amp;#8217;s&#13;identification of its performance obligations in a contract, as well as an entity&amp;#8217;s evaluation of the nature of its promise&#13;to grant a license of intellectual property and whether or not that revenue is recognized over time or at a point in time. This&#13;ASU has the same effective date as the new revenue standard, which is effective for fiscal years, and for interim periods within&#13;those fiscal years, beginning after December 15, 2017. The Company is considering the alternatives of adoption of this ASU and&#13;will continue to review the likely impact to the existing portfolio of customer contracts entered into prior to adoption. The Company&#13;will continue to evaluate the effect of adopting this guidance upon its results of operations, cash flows and financial position.&#13;The Company does not expect the adoption of this ASU to have a material impact on its consolidated financial statements except&#13;that there are significant additional reporting requirements under the new standard.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;In May 2016, the FASB issued ASU 2016-11, Revenue&#13;Recognition (Topic 605) and Derivatives and Hedging (Topic 815): Rescission of SEC Guidance Because of Accounting Standards Updates&#13;2014-09 and 2014-16 Pursuant to Staff Announcements at the March 3, 2016 EITF Meeting. This ASU rescinds SEC paragraphs pursuant&#13;to two SEC Staff Announcements at the March 3, 2016 Emerging Issues Task Force (EITF) meeting. Specifically, registrants should&#13;not rely on the following SEC Staff Observer comments upon adoption of Topic 606: (1) Revenue and Expense Recognition for Freight&#13;Services in Process, which is codified in paragraph 605-20-S99-2; (2) Accounting for Shipping and Handling Fees and Costs, which&#13;is codified in paragraph 605-45-S99-1; (3) Accounting for Consideration Given by a Vendor to a Customer (including Reseller of&#13;the Vendor&amp;#8217;s Products), which is codified in paragraph 605-50-S99-1; and (4) Accounting for Gas-Balancing Arrangements (i.e.,&#13;use of the &amp;#8220;entitlements method&amp;#8221;), which is codified in paragraph 932-10-S99-5. This ASU becomes effective upon adoption&#13;of ASU 2014-09, which is effective for fiscal years, and for interim periods within those fiscal years, beginning after December&#13;15, 2017. The Company has not yet begun to consider the alternatives of adoption of this ASU or its impact on its consolidated&#13;financial statements.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;In May 2016, the FASB issued ASU 2016-12, Revenue&#13;from Contracts with Customers (Topic 606): Narrow-Scope Improvements and Practical Expedients. This ASU does not change the core&#13;principle of the guidance in Topic 606. Instead, the amendments provide clarifying guidance in a few narrow areas and add some&#13;practical expedients to the guidance. This ASU has the same effective date as the new revenue standard, which is effective for&#13;fiscal years, and for interim periods within those fiscal years, beginning after December 15, 2017. The Company is currently evaluating&#13;the impact of the pending adoption of this new standard on its consolidated financial statements. The Company is considering the&#13;alternatives of adoption of this ASU. Currently, the Company does not expect the adoption of this ASU to have a material impact&#13;on its financial statements except that there are significant additional reporting requirements under the new standard.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;In August 2016, the FASB issued ASU 2016-15,&#13;Statement of Cash Flows (Topic 230): Classification of Certain Cash Receipts and Cash Payments. The new guidance is intended to&#13;reduce diversity in practice in how transactions are classified in the statement of cash flows. This ASU is effective for fiscal&#13;years, and for interim periods within those fiscal years, beginning after December 15, 2017. Early adoption is permitted. The Company&#13;is currently evaluating the impact of this ASU on its consolidated financial statements and currently the Company has determined&#13;there to be no impact of this ASU on its financial statements and related disclosures.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;The accompanying consolidated financial statements&#13;have been prepared assuming the Company will continue as a going concern, which contemplates, among other things, the realization&#13;of assets and satisfaction of liabilities in the normal course of business. Since inception, the Company has financed its operations&#13;primarily through equity and debt financings. As of December 31, 2017 and 2016, the Company had an accumulated deficit of $10,500,883&#13;and $6,964,957 (all of which was attributed to the losses of B&amp;#250;cha, Inc., and one-time expenses associated with the integration&#13;and up-listing onto the NASDAQ exchange and acquisitions of Maverick, PMC, Marley during the year ended December 31, 2017 and Xing&#13;during the year ended December 31, 2016). For the years ended December 31, 2017 and 2016, respectively, cash flows from operating&#13;activities were ($8,410,777) and $975,176.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times

Xing is engaged&#13;in the manufacturing and sale of various teas and beverages, which will help the Company expand its capabilities and product offering.&#13;The operating results of Xing have been consolidated with those of the Company beginning July 1, 2016. Total purchase consideration&#13;paid was $19,995,000, which consisted of $8,500,000 of cash, a note payable for $4,500,000 and 4,353,915 shares of common stock.&#13;The common stock issued was valued at $1.61 per share, which was the volume weighted average closing stock for the thirty days&#13;preceding the acquisition.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman

The operating results of Maverick&#13;have been consolidated with those of the Company beginning April 1, 2017. The common stock issued was valued at&#13;$4.13 per share, which was the closing stock on the date of the acquisition. The Acquisition was subject to customary closing conditions.&#13;All of the goodwill was assigned to the Company&amp;#8217;s Brands segment. All of the goodwill and intangible assets recognized is&#13;expected to be deductible for income tax purposes. The fair value of the customer list was valued using the income approach, as&#13;the Company obtained an independent third-party valuation. In addition, the market approach was utilized to determine the fair&#13;value of the trade name and recipes.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman

   &lt;td style=border-bottom: black 1pt double; text-align: right&gt;&lt;font style=font-size: 8pt&gt;11,086,000&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=padding-bottom: 3pt&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&#13;&lt;/table&gt;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman

 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;Goodwill is the excess of the purchase price&#13;over the preliminary fair value of the underlying net tangible and identifiable intangible assets. In accordance with applicable&#13;accounting standards, goodwill is not amortized but instead is tested for impairment at least annually or more frequently if certain&#13;indicators are present.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;In connection with the acquisition of Maverick,&#13;the Company incurred transactional costs totaling $231,925, which has been recognized as expense for the year ended December 31,&#13;2017. These costs have been reflected in other expenses.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&lt;b&gt;&lt;i&gt;PMC Holdings, Inc.&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;On May 18, 2017, the Company entered into an&#13;Asset Purchase Agreement (the &amp;#8220;Agreement&amp;#8221;) whereby the Company acquired substantially all of the operating assets of&#13;Premier Micronutrient Corporation, a subsidiary of PMC Holdings, Inc. (&amp;#8220;PMC&amp;#8221;), which is a company engaged in the business&#13;of developing, manufacturing, selling and marketing micronutrient products and formulations (the &amp;#8220;Acquisition&amp;#8221;). On&#13;May 23, 2017 (the &amp;#8220;Closing Date&amp;#8221;), the parties executed the Bill of Sale and Assignment and Assumption Agreement for&#13;the Acquisition.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;Upon the Closing Date, the Company received&#13;substantially all of the operating assets of PMC, consisting of fixed assets and intellectual property in exchange for a purchase&#13;price of 1,200,000 shares of the Company&amp;#8217;s common stock. The shares were fair valued at $4.58 per share. The Company also&#13;agreed to assume various accounts payable and accrued liabilities of PMC. The shares of Common Stock to be issued pursuant to the&#13;Acquisition will be restricted under Rule 144. The Acquisition was subject to customary closing conditions. All of the goodwill&#13;was assigned to the Company&amp;#8217;s Brands segment. All of the goodwill and intangible assets recognized is expected to be deductible&#13;for income tax purposes. The fair value of the patents were valued using the market approach, as the Company obtained an independent&#13;third-party valuation.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times

 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;In connection with the acquisition of PMC, the&#13;Company incurred minimal transactional costs, which has been recognized as expense as of the closing date.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&lt;b&gt;&lt;i&gt;Marley Beverage Company, LLC&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;On March 23, 2017, the Company entered into&#13;an asset purchase agreement (the &amp;#8220;APA&amp;#8221;) whereby the Company agreed to acquire substantially all of the operating assets&#13;of Marley Beverage Company, LLC (&amp;#8220;Marley&amp;#8221;), which is a company engaged in the development, manufacturing, selling and&#13;marketing of nonalcoholic relaxation teas and sparkling waters, and ready to drink coffee drinks. The consideration for the Acquisition&#13;was amended pursuant to an Amendment to the APA dated June 9, 2017. The Acquisition closed on June 13, 2017.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;At closing, the Company received substantially&#13;all of the operating assets of Marley, consisting of inventory, accounts receivable, fixed assets and intellectual property in&#13;exchange for a purchase price of 3,000,000 shares of the Company&amp;#8217;s common stock, as well as an earn out payment of $1,250,000&#13;in cash if the gross revenues of the Marley business during any trailing twelve calendar month period after the closing are equal&#13;to or greater than $15,000,000. The earnout, if applicable, will be paid as $625,000 on or before the 15th day after the end of&#13;the first trailing twelve calendar month period in which the earnout condition is satisfied, $312,500 not later than the first&#13;anniversary of the initial earnout payment, and $312,500 not later than the second anniversary of the initial earnout payment.&#13;The fair value of the earnout was valued using the weighted average return on asset. The shares of Common Stock issued pursuant&#13;to the Acquisition have not been registered, but the holders have piggyback registration rights, as well as demand registration&#13;rights, with the demand registration rights beginning twelve months from the Closing Date. The Acquisition was subject to customary&#13;closing conditions. The shares were fair valued at $6.20 per share. All of the goodwill was assigned to the Company&amp;#8217;s Brands&#13;segment. All of the goodwill and intangible assets recognized is expected to be deductible for income tax purposes. The fair value&#13;of the customer list was valued using the cost approach, as the Company obtained an independent third-party valuation. In addition,&#13;the market approach was utilized to determine the fair value of the trade name and recipes.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times

 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;The following unaudited pro forma financial&#13;results reflects the historical operating results of the Company, including the unaudited pro forma results of Xing Group, Maverick,&#13;PMC and Marley for the years ended December 31, 2017 and 2016, respectively, as if Xing Group, Maverick, PMC and Marley were acquired&#13;on January 1, 2016.  Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;Inventories consist of brewing materials, tea&#13;ingredients, bulk packaging and finished goods. The cost elements of work in process and finished goods inventory consist of raw&#13;materials and direct labor. Provisions for excess inventory are included in cost of goods sold and have historically been immaterial&#13;but adequate to provide for losses on its raw materials. Inventories are stated at the lower of cost, determined on the first-in,&#13;first-out basis, or market.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman

text-align: right&gt;&lt;font style=font-size: 8pt&gt;10,374,675&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=padding-bottom: 3pt&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&#13;&lt;/table&gt;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman

 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;In connection with the Acquisition of Xing,&#13;the Company entered into several notes payable with a bank and received proceeds of $10.7 million. One note payable is for $4,800,000,&#13;bears interest at 4.04%, and is secured by the Company&amp;#8217;s land and building. Principal and interest is payable in monthly&#13;installments of $25,495 through June 2021 at which time the unpaid principal balance is due. The other note payable is a revolving&#13;credit facility that allows borrows up to $5.9 million, bears interest payable monthly at LIBOR plus a margin ranging from 2.25%&#13;to 3.00% depending on the current ratio of payment obligations to earnings as defined in the agreement, and is secured by the Company&amp;#8217;s&#13;assets. The amount that may be borrowed under the revolving credit facility is based on the Company&amp;#8217;s eligible receivables,&#13;inventory and fixed assets, and is reduces by $50,000 each month beginning August 1, 2016 until the facility has been reduced down&#13;to $2,900,000. The revolving credit facility matures on June 30, 2018. As of December 31, 2017 and 2016, there are no available&#13;borrowings under the revolving credit facility.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;The Company also issued a $4,500,000 note payable&#13;to a selling shareholder of Xing. This seller&amp;#8217;s note bears interest, payable monthly, at 1% per year, beginning after December&#13;31, 2016. The loan matures on June 30, 2017.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;On March 19, 2016, the Company entered into&#13;a Securities Purchase Agreement with an unaffiliated third party, whereby the Company sold a Convertible Promissory Note in an&#13;amount of $200,000. The purchaser also received a three-year Warrant to purchase 100,000 shares at an exercise price of $0.40 per&#13;share. The Company has allocated the loan proceeds among the debt and the warrant based upon relative fair values. The relative&#13;fair value of the warrant was determined to be $18,153.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;In connection with the Acquisition of Maverick,&#13;the Company assumed Series B notes payable of $1,472,051. In addition, in connection with the public offering of common stock in&#13;February 2017, proceeds were used to reduce the previously outstanding note balances. Monthly payments consist of interest only&#13;payments. The loans are due December 2018.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;On July 6, 2017 the Company entered into&#13;a revolving credit agreement with U.S. Bank National Association. Total borrowings were $2,000,000 and are subject to&#13;borrowing base requirements per the agreement. The credit agreement bears interest at 2.5% plus Daily Reset LIBOR Rate.&#13;Currently, interest only payments of approximately $7,000 monthly. The loan matures July 6, 2018 and the entire principal&#13;and outstanding interest payments are due. The revolving credit line is subject to a fixed charged ratio financial covenant.&#13;The Company must maintain a fixed charged coverage ratio of at least 1:15 to 1:00. As of and for the year ended December 31,&#13;2017, the Company was in compliance with this financial covenant.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;Related Party debt consisted of the following&#13;as of:&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman

 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;In March 2015, the Company borrowed $60,000&#13;from a member of management. The note bears interest at 10% per annum and is due and payable beginning June 30, 2015 maturing on&#13;March 31, 2020. Payments of interest are required quarterly. The note was issued in conjunction with an equity payment totaling&#13;53,073 shares of Series B preferred stock that was issued with the debt. The Company has allocated the loan proceeds among the&#13;debt and the stock based upon relative fair values. The relative fair value of the stock was determined to be $42,742 and was recorded&#13;as a debt discount. The discount is being amortized over the life of the loan to interest expense. As of December 31, 2016, no&#13;principal payment has been made on this note (but has since been paid in full in February 2017). No amounts were outstanding as&#13;of December 31, 2017.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&lt;i&gt;Operating Lease Commitments&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;On June 30, 2016, the Company assumed the lease&#13;commitments for the New Age Beverage, LLC (NAB) and Xing Beverage, LLC (Xing) when it acquired those companies. The Colorado Springs&#13;property, previously leased by Xing, has a base rent of $14,000 per month plus common area expenses, with escalation clauses over&#13;time. On January 10, 2017, the Company entered into a Purchase and Sale Agreement with an unaffiliated third party. Pursuant to&#13;the agreement, the Company entered into a commitment to sell the property located at 1700 E 68th Avenue, Denver, CO 80229 for a&#13;purchase price of $8,900,000. The agreement contains a lease back provision, whereby the Company leases the property for an initial&#13;term of ten years, with an option to extend for two successive five-year periods. The Company recognized a gain on the sale of&#13;this property of $3,272,653 (as reflected on the Consolidated Statement of Operations under the caption &amp;#8220;Other Income&amp;#8221;)&#13;for the year ended December 31, 2017. The Company early adopted the provisions of ASU 2016-02. The lease cost is $52,000 per month&#13;for the initial year, with two percent annual increases. Management elected to early adopt ASU 2016-02, as a result, the Company&#13;recognized a Right-of-Use for the asset of approximately $4,500,000 and a corresponding liability of a similar amount.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times

The purpose&#13;of the Plan is to provide such individuals with additional incentive and reward opportunities designed to enhance the profitable&#13;growth of the Company and its affiliates. The shares of common stock to be issued in connection with the Plan will not be registered&#13;under the Securities Act.
