 Times
 Serif; margin: 0&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0&gt;The Company files income tax returns in the U.S. Federal jurisdiction&#13;and various state jurisdictions.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0&gt;Income taxes are accounted for under the asset and liability method.&#13;Deferred tax assets and liabilities are recognized for the future tax consequences attributable to differences between the financial&#13;statement carrying amounts of existing assets and liabilities and their respective tax bases and operating loss and tax credit&#13;carryforwards. Deferred tax assets and liabilities are measured using enacted tax rates expected to apply to taxable income in&#13;the years in which those temporary differences are expected to be recovered or settled. The Company must assess the likelihood&#13;that its deferred tax assets will be recovered from future taxable income and, to the extent that it is more likely than not that&#13;such deferred tax assets will not be realized, the Company must establish a valuation allowance.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0&gt;As of December 31, 2017 and 2016, the Company has a valuation allowance&#13;against 100% of the deferred tax assets, which is primarily composed of net operating loss (or &lt;i&gt;NOL&lt;/i&gt;) carryforwards. Even&#13;though the Company has reserved all of these net deferred tax assets for book purposes, the Company would still be able to utilize&#13;them to reduce future income taxes payable should the Company have future taxable earnings. To the extent the deferred tax assets&#13;relate to NOL carryforwards, the ability to use such NOLs against future earnings will be subject to applicable carryforward periods.&#13;As of December 31, 2017 and 2016, the Company had NOL carryforwards for both Federal and state tax purposes of approximately $10.9&#13;million, which are available to offset taxable income through 2037. Our NOL carryforwards begin to expire in 2028.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0&gt;In December 2017, the Tax Cuts and Jobs Act (the &amp;#8220;2017 Tax&#13;Act&amp;#8221;) was enacted. The 2017 Tax Act includes a number of changes to existing U.S. tax laws that impact the Company, most&#13;notably a reduction of the U.S. corporate income tax rate from 35 percent to 21 percent for tax years beginning after December&#13;31, 2017. The 2017 Tax Act also provides for a one-time transition tax on certain foreign earnings and the acceleration of depreciation&#13;for certain assets placed into service after September 27, 2017 as well as prospective changes beginning in 2018, including changing&#13;rules related to uses and limitations of net operating loss carryforwards created in tax years beginning after December 31, 2017.&#13;Specifically, the 2017 Tax Act limits the amount the Company is able to deduct for net operating loss carryforwards generated in&#13;taxable years beginning after December 31, 2017 to 80% of taxable income however these net operating loss carryforwards can be&#13;carried forward indefinitely, repeal of the domestic manufacturing deduction, acceleration of tax revenue recognition, capitalization&#13;of research and development expenditures, additional limitations on executive compensation and limitations on the deductibility&#13;of interest.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0&gt;The changes to existing U.S. tax laws as a result of the 2017 Tax&#13;Act, which the Company believes has the most significant impact on the Company&amp;#8217;s federal income taxes are as follows:&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0&gt;&lt;i&gt;Reduction of the U.S. Corporate Income Tax Rate&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0&gt;The Company measures deferred tax assets and liabilities using enacted&#13;tax rates that will apply in the years in which the temporary differences are expected to be recovered or paid. Accordingly, the&#13;Company&amp;#8217;s deferred tax assets and liabilities were remeasured to reflect the reduction in the U.S. corporate income tax&#13;rate from 35 percent to 21 percent, resulting in a $1.4 million decrease in net deferred tax assets and a corresponding $1.4 million&#13;decrease in the valuation allowance as of December 31, 2017.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0&gt;For the years ended December 31, 2017 and December 31, 2016, there&#13;was no income tax expense recognized. &lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;The Company follows segment reporting in accordance&#13;with FASB ASC Topic 280, &lt;i&gt;Segment Reporting&lt;/i&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;Management views its operations based on two&#13;distinct reporting segments: (1) the Direct Store Distributions (DSD) and (2) the Brands segment. Operations and net assets that&#13;are not associated with any of these operating segments are reported as &amp;#8220;Corporate&amp;#8221; when disclosing and discussing&#13;segment information.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;The DSD segment distributes beverages throughout&#13;Colorado and surrounding states, delivering to approximately 6,000 retail customers.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;The Brands segment sells beverages to wholesale&#13;distributors, broadliners, key account owned warehouses and international accounts using several distribution channels.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times

&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;During February 2018 the Company converted its&#13;Series B Preferred Stock at a ratio of 8:1 into 1,353,872 shares of common stock.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;On March 12, 2018 the Company granted and issued&#13;a total of 122,640 shares to members of the board of directors for services rendered.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;On April 10, 2018, the Company, entered&#13;into an underwriting agreement (the &amp;#8220;Underwriting Agreement&amp;#8221;) with Euro Pacific Capital, Inc., doing business as&#13;A.G.P./Alliance Global Partners acting as representative of the several underwriters (the &amp;#8220;Underwriters&amp;#8221;), which&#13;provided for the issuance and sale by the Company in an underwritten public offering (the &amp;#8220;Offering&amp;#8221;) and the&#13;purchase by the Underwriters of 2,285,715 shares of the Company&amp;#8217;s common stock, $0.001 par value per share. Subject to&#13;the terms and conditions contained in the Underwriting Agreement, the shares were sold to the Underwriters at a public&#13;offering price of $1.75 per share, less certain underwriting discounts and commissions. The Company also granted the&#13;Underwriters a 45 day option to purchase, severally and not jointly, up to 342,857 additional shares of the Company&amp;#8217;s&#13;common stock on the same terms and conditions for the purpose of covering any over-allotments in connection with the&#13;Offering. The net offering proceeds to the Company from the Offering are estimated to be approximately $3.5 million, after&#13;deducting estimated underwriting discounts and commissions and other estimated offering expenses. The Company intends to use&#13;the net proceeds from the Offering for purchasing inventory for newly gained distribution and other general working capital&#13;purposes.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;Our consolidated financial statements include&#13;the accounts of all majority-owned subsidiary companies. All intercompany transactions and balances have been eliminated.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;The preparation of the consolidated financial&#13;statements in conformity with U.S. GAAP requires management to make estimates and assumptions that affect the reported amounts&#13;of assets and liabilities and disclosure of contingent assets and liabilities at the date of the consolidated financial statements&#13;and the reported amounts of revenue and expenses during the reporting period. Actual results could differ from those estimates.&#13;The more significant estimates and assumptions made by management include allowance for doubtful accounts, inventory valuation,&#13;provision for excess or expired inventory, depreciation of property and equipment, realizability of long-lived assets, allowance&#13;for sales returns and chargebacks, estimated cash flows in the acquisitions, and fair market value of equity instruments issued&#13;for goods or services. The current economic environment has increased the degree and uncertainty inherent in these estimates and&#13;assumptions.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; color: #231F20&gt;Cash and cash equivalents as&#13;of December 31, 2017 and 2016 included cash on-hand. Cash equivalents are considered all accounts with an original maturity date&#13;within 90 days.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;The Company&amp;#8217;s accounts receivable&#13;primarily consists of trade receivables. The Company records an allowance for doubtful accounts that is based on historical&#13;trends, customer knowledge, any known disputes, and the aging of the accounts receivable balances combined with&#13;management&amp;#8217;s estimate of future potential recoverability. Receivables are written off against the allowance after all&#13;attempts to collect a receivable have failed. The Company&amp;#8217;s allowance for doubtful accounts was $52,345 as of December&#13;31, 2017 and $46,350 as of December 31, 2016.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;Financial instruments that potentially subject&#13;the Company to concentrations of credit risk consist principally of cash and accounts receivables.&amp;#160; The Company places its&#13;cash with high credit quality financial institutions.&amp;#160; At times such amounts may exceed federally insured limits.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;For the year ended December 31, 2017, three&#13;customers represented approximately 21.4% (9.9%, 6.3% and 5.2%) of net revenues. For the year ended December 31, 2016, three customers&#13;represented approximately 27.5% (14.5%, 7.5% and 5.5%) of net revenues. As of December 31, 2017, three customers represented 23.1%&#13;(10.5%, 6.7% and 5.9%) of accounts receivables. As of December 31, 2016, three customers represented approximately 29.4% (12.3%,&#13;8.9% and 8.2%) of accounts receivable.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; color: #231F20&gt;Goodwill represents the excess&#13;of the purchase price of acquired businesses over the estimated fair value of the identifiable net assets acquired. Goodwill and&#13;other intangibles with indefinite useful lives are not amortized but tested for impairment annually or more frequently when events&#13;or circumstances indicates that the carrying value of a reporting unit more likely than not exceeds its fair value. The goodwill&#13;impairment test is applied by performing a qualitative assessment before calculating the fair value of the reporting unit. If,&#13;on the basis of qualitative factors, it is considered not more likely than not that the fair value of the reporting unit is less&#13;than the carrying amount, further testing of goodwill for impairment would not be required. If the carrying amount of a reporting&#13;unit exceeds the reporting unit&amp;#8217;s fair value, an impairment loss is recognized in an amount equal to that excess, limited&#13;to the total amount of goodwill allocated to that reporting unit. The Company performed a qualitative assessment and determined&#13;there was no impairment of goodwill for the years ended December 31, 2017 and 2016.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;Intangible assets are recorded at acquisition&#13;fair value as part of the acquisitions. The balance as of December 31, 2017 and 2016 is reflected net of accumulated amortization.&#13;Definite lived intangible assets are amortized over their estimated useful life using the straight-line method, which is determined&#13;by identifying the period over which the cash flows from the asset are expected to be generated, typically 15 to 42 years. As of&#13;December 31, 2017 and 2016 accumulated amortization was $1,368,568 and $340,126, respectively. Amortization expense was $1,028,443&#13;and $340,126 for the years ended December 31, 2017 and 2016, respectively.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;Long-lived assets consisted of property and&#13;equipment and customer relationships and are reviewed for impairment in accordance with the guidance of the ASC 360, Property,&#13;Plant, and Equipment. The Company tests for impairment losses on long-lived assets used in operations whenever events or changes&#13;in circumstances indicate that the carrying amount of the asset may not be recoverable. For the years ended December 31, 2017 and&#13;2016, respectively, the Company had not experienced impairment losses on the long-lived assets as management determined that there&#13;were no indicators that the carrying amount of the asset may not be recoverable.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;Inventories consist of tea ingredients, packaging&#13;and finished goods and are stated at the lower of cost (first-in, first-out basis) or market value.&amp;#160; Provisions for excess&#13;inventory are included in cost of goods sold and have historically been immaterial but adequate to provide for losses on its raw&#13;materials.&amp;#160; There was no reserve for obsolescence as of December 31, 2017 and December 31, 2016.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;Property and equipment consists primarily of&#13;brewing equipment and are stated at cost.&amp;#160; Depreciation is computed using the straight-line method based upon the estimated&#13;useful lives of the underlying assets, generally five years.&amp;#160; Major renewals and betterments that extend the life of the property&#13;are capitalized.&amp;#160; Expenditures for repairs and maintenance are expensed as incurred.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;Customer programs and incentives, which include&#13;customer promotional discount programs and customer incentives, are a common practice in the beverage industry.&amp;#160; The Company&#13;incurs customer program costs to promote sales of products and to maintain competitive pricing.&amp;#160; Amounts paid in connection&#13;with customer programs and incentives are recorded as reductions to net revenue or as advertising, promotional and selling expenses&#13;in accordance with ASC Topic 605-50, &lt;i&gt;Revenue Recognition&amp;#8212;Customer Payments and Incentives&lt;/i&gt;, based on the nature of&#13;the expenditure.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;Cost of goods sold mainly consisted of raw material&#13;costs, packaging costs and direct labor.&amp;#160; Costs are recognized when the related revenue is recorded.&amp;#160; Shipping and handling&#13;costs for all wholesale sales transactions are billed to the customer and are included in costs of goods sold for all periods presented.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;Advertising, promotional and selling expenses&#13;consisted of sales salaries, tap handles, media advertising costs, sales and marketing expenses, and promotional activity expenses&#13;and are recognized when incurred in the accompanying consolidated statements of operations.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;General and administrative expenses consisted&#13;of professional service fees, rent and utility expenses, meals, travel and entertainment expenses, and other general and administrative&#13;overhead costs.&amp;#160; Expenses are recognized when incurred.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;The Company accounts for income taxes pursuant&#13;to the provisions of ASC 740, &lt;i&gt;Income Taxes&lt;/i&gt;, whereby deferred tax assets and liabilities are recognized for the future tax&#13;consequences attributable to differences between the financial statement carrying amount of existing assets and liabilities and&#13;their respective tax bases and the future tax benefits derived from operating loss and tax credit carryforwards. The Company provides&#13;a valuation allowance on our deferred tax assets when it is more likely than not that such deferred tax assets will not be realized.&#13;The Company has a valuation allowance against 100% of the net deferred tax assets.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 27pt&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;ASC 740 requires that the Company recognize&#13;in the consolidated financial statements the effect of a tax position that is more likely than not to be sustained upon examination&#13;based on the technical merits of the position. The first step is to determine whether or not a tax benefit should be recognized.&#13;A tax benefit will be recognized if the weight of available evidence indicates that the tax position is more likely than not to&#13;be sustained upon examination by the relevant tax authorities. The recognition and measurement of benefits related to our tax positions&#13;requires significant judgment as uncertainties often exist with respect to new laws, new interpretations of existing laws, and&#13;rulings by taxing authorities. Differences between actual results and our assumptions, or changes in our assumptions in future&#13;periods, are recorded in the period they become known. For tax liabilities, the Company recognizes accrued interest related to&#13;uncertain tax positions as a component of income tax expense, and penalties, if incurred, are recognized as a component of operating&#13;expense.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;Basic net income (loss) per share is calculated&#13;by dividing net income (loss) by the weighted-average common shares outstanding.&amp;#160; Diluted net income per share is calculated&#13;by dividing net income by the weighted-average common shares outstanding during the period using the treasury stock method or the&#13;two-class method, whichever is more dilutive.&amp;#160; As the Company incurred net losses for the periods ended December 31, 2017&#13;and 2016 no potentially dilutive securities were included in the calculation of diluted earnings per share as the impact would&#13;have been anti-dilutive.&amp;#160; Therefore, basic and dilutive net income (loss) per share were the same.&amp;#160; If the Company had&#13;net income, potential dilutive securities consist of warrants to purchase zero and 1,127,000 shares of common stock as of December&#13;31, 2017 and December 31, 2016, respectively.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times

   &lt;td style=width: 75%&gt;&lt;font style=font-size: 8pt&gt;Revenues&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=width: 1%&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=width: 1%&gt;&lt;font style=font-size: 8pt&gt;$&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=width: 9%; text-align: right&gt;&lt;font style=font-size: 8pt&gt;14,643&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=width: 1%&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=width: 1%&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=width: 1%&gt;&lt;font style=font-size: 8pt&gt;$&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=width: 9%; text-align: right&gt;&lt;font style=font-size: 8pt&gt;7,091&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=width: 2%&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&#13;&lt;tr style=vertical-align: bottom&gt;&#13;    &lt;td&gt;&lt;font style=font-size: 8pt&gt;Cost of sales&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=padding-bottom: 1.5pt&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=border-bottom: black 1pt solid&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=border-bottom: black 1pt solid; text-align: right&gt;&lt;font style=font-size: 8pt&gt;(11,692&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=padding-bottom: 1.5pt&gt;&lt;font style=font-size: 8pt&gt;)&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=padding-bottom: 1.5pt&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=border-bottom: black 1pt solid&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=border-bottom: black 1pt solid; text-align: right&gt;&lt;font style=font-size: 8pt&gt;(4,580&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=padding-bottom: 1.5pt&gt;&lt;font style=font-size: 8pt&gt;)&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&#13;&lt;tr style=vertical-align: bottom&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=padding-left: 0.25in&gt;&lt;font style=font-size: 8pt&gt;Gross profit&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=padding-bottom: 3pt&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=border-bottom: black 1pt double&gt;&lt;font style=font-size: 8pt&gt;$&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=border-bottom: black 1pt double; text-align: right&gt;&lt;font style=font-size: 8pt&gt;2,951&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=padding-bottom: 3pt&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=padding-bottom: 3pt&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=border-bottom: black 1pt double&gt;&lt;font style=font-size: 8pt&gt;$&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=border-bottom: black 1pt double; text-align: right&gt;&lt;font style=font-size: 8pt&gt;2,511&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=padding-bottom: 3pt&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&#13;&lt;/table&gt;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;The carrying amount of the financial instruments,&#13;which principally include cash, trade receivables, accounts payable and accrued expenses, approximates fair value due to the relative&#13;short maturity of such instruments. The carrying amount of the Company&amp;#8217;s debt approximates its fair value as it bears interest&#13;at market rates of interest after taking into consideration the debt discounts.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 27pt&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;Accounting Standards Codification (ASC) 820&#13;defines fair value, establishes a framework for measuring fair value under U.S. GAAP and enhances disclosures about fair value&#13;measurements. Fair value is defined under ASC 820 as the exchange price that would be received for an asset or paid to transfer&#13;a liability (an exit price) in the principal or most advantageous market for the asset or liability in an orderly transaction between&#13;market participants on the measurement date. Valuation techniques used to measure fair value under ASC 820 must maximize the use&#13;of observable inputs and minimize the use of unobservable inputs. The standard describes a fair-value hierarchy based on three&#13;levels of inputs, of which the first two are considered observable and the last unobservable, that may be used to measure fair&#13;value as follows:&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 27pt&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 27pt&gt;&lt;b&gt;&lt;i&gt;Level 1&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/b&gt;&amp;#8212;Quoted&#13;prices in active markets for identical assets or liabilities.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 27pt&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 27pt&gt;&lt;b&gt;&lt;i&gt;Level 2&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/b&gt;&amp;#8212;Inputs&#13;other than Level 1 that are observable, either directly or indirectly, such as quoted prices for similar assets or liabilities;&#13;quoted prices in markets that are not active; or other inputs that are observable or can be corroborated by observable market data&#13;for substantially the full term of the assets or liabilities.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 27pt&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 27pt&gt;&lt;b&gt;&lt;i&gt;Level 3&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/b&gt;&amp;#8212;Unobservable&#13;inputs that are supported by little or no market activity and that are significant to the fair value of the assets or liabilities.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 27pt&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 10pt 0 0; text-indent: 24.5pt&gt;The following tables set forth the fair&#13;value of the Company&amp;#8217;s contingent provision as of December&amp;#160;31, 2017 and 2016:&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times

 Serif&gt;&amp;#160;&amp;#160;&amp;#160;&amp;#160;&amp;#160;&amp;#160;&amp;#160;&amp;#160;&amp;#160;&amp;#160;&amp;#160;&amp;#160;-&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=vertical-align: bottom&gt;&lt;font style=font: 8pt Times New Roman

 Serif&gt;&amp;#160;&amp;#160;&amp;#160;&amp;#160;&amp;#160;&amp;#160;&amp;#160;&amp;#160;-&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td nowrap=nowrap style=vertical-align: bottom&gt;&lt;font style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=vertical-align: bottom&gt;&lt;font style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif&gt;$&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=vertical-align: bottom; text-align: right&gt;&lt;font style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif&gt;-&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td&gt;&lt;font style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&#13;&lt;/table&gt;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0&gt;&lt;font style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=margin: 0&gt;&lt;font style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;In May 2014, the FASB issued ASU No. 2014-09,&#13;Revenue from Contracts with Customers, as a new Topic, ASC Topic 606.&amp;#160;The new revenue recognition standard provides a five-step&#13;analysis of transactions to determine when and how revenue is recognized.&amp;#160;The core principle is that a company should recognize&#13;revenue to depict the transfer of promised goods or services to customers in an amount that reflects the consideration to which&#13;the entity expects to be entitled in exchange for those goods or services. In August 2015, the FASB issued ASU No. 2015-14, Revenue&#13;from Contracts with Customers: Deferral of the Effective Date, which deferred the effective date of the new revenue standard for&#13;periods beginning after December 15, 2016 to December 15, 2017, with early adoption permitted but not earlier than the original&#13;effective date. This ASU must be applied retrospectively to each period presented or as a cumulative-effect adjustment as of the&#13;date of adoption.&amp;#160;The Company is considering the alternatives of adoption of this ASU and is conducting its review of the&#13;likely impact to the existing portfolio of customer contracts entered into prior to adoption. After completing its review, the&#13;Company will continue to evaluate the effect of adopting this guidance upon the Company results of operations, cash flows and financial&#13;position. Currently, the Company does not expect the adoption of this ASU to have a material impact on its financial statements&#13;except that there are significant additional reporting requirements under the new standard.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;In February 2016, the FASB issued ASU No. 2016-02,&#13;Leases. This ASU establishes a right-of-use (ROU) model that requires a lessee to record a ROU asset and a lease liability on the&#13;balance sheet for all leases with terms longer than 12 months. Leases will be classified as either finance or operating, with classification&#13;affecting the pattern of expense recognition in the income statement. This ASU is effective for fiscal years beginning after December&#13;15, 2018, including interim periods within those fiscal years. A modified retrospective transition approach is required for lessees&#13;for capital and operating leases existing at, or entered into after, the beginning of the earliest comparative period presented&#13;in the financial statements, with certain practical expedients available. During the year ended December 31, 2017 management elected&#13;to early adopt the guidance under ASU 2016-02. Management&amp;#8217;s decision was based on the stock price during the year would most&#13;likely result in the Company entering into and being designated an accelerated filer by June 30, 2019, which would result in management&#13;having to restate the financial statements to reflect the adoption of the new standard.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 27pt&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;In March 2016, the FASB issued ASU 2016-08,&#13;Revenue from Contracts with Customers (Topic 606). This ASU is related to reporting revenue gross versus net, or principal versus&#13;agent considerations. This ASU is meant to clarify the guidance in ASU 2014-09,&amp;#160;Revenue from Contracts with Customers, as&#13;it pertains to principal versus agent considerations. Specifically, the guidance addresses how entities should identify goods and&#13;services being provided to a customer, the unit of account for a principal versus agent assessment, how to evaluate whether a good&#13;or service is controlled before being transferred to a customer, and how to assess whether an entity controls services performed&#13;by another party. This ASU has the same effective date as the new revenue standard, which is effective for fiscal years, and for&#13;interim periods within those fiscal years, beginning after December 15, 2017. The Company is evaluating the effect and methodology&#13;of adopting this new accounting guidance upon the Company results of operations, cash flows and financial position. The Company&#13;has begun to consider the alternatives of adoption of this ASU, and has started its review of the likely impact to the existing&#13;portfolio of customer contracts entered into prior to adoption. The Company will also continue to evaluate the effect of adopting&#13;this guidance upon its results of operations, cash flows and financial position. Currently, the Company does not expect the adoption&#13;of this ASU to have a material impact on its consolidated financial statements except that there are significant additional reporting&#13;requirements under the new standard.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: center&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;In March 2016, the FASB issued ASU&#13;2016-09, Compensation-Stock Compensation (Topic 718). This ASU is related to simplifications of employee share-based payment&#13;accounting. This pronouncement eliminates the APIC pool concept and requires that excess tax benefits and tax deficiencies be&#13;recorded in the income statement when awards are settled. The pronouncement also addresses simplifications related to&#13;statement of cash flows classification, accounting for forfeitures and minimum statutory tax withholding requirements. This&#13;ASU is effective for fiscal years, and for interim periods within those fiscal years, beginning after December 15, 2016.&#13;    This ASU does  not have a material impact on the Company&amp;#8217;s consolidated financial&#13;statements based on managements conclusion.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;In April 2016, the FASB issued ASU 2016-10,&#13;Revenue from Contracts with Customers (Topic 606): Identifying Performance Obligations and Licensing. This ASU is meant to clarify&#13;the guidance in FASB ASU 2014-09,&amp;#160;Revenue from Contracts with Customers. Specifically, the guidance addresses an entity&amp;#8217;s&#13;identification of its performance obligations in a contract, as well as an entity&amp;#8217;s evaluation of the nature of its promise&#13;to grant a license of intellectual property and whether or not that revenue is recognized over time or at a point in time. This&#13;ASU has the same effective date as the new revenue standard, which is effective for fiscal years, and for interim periods within&#13;those fiscal years, beginning after December 15, 2017. The Company is considering the alternatives of adoption of this ASU and&#13;will continue to review the likely impact to the existing portfolio of customer contracts entered into prior to adoption. The Company&#13;will continue to evaluate the effect of adopting this guidance upon its results of operations, cash flows and financial position.&#13;The Company does not expect the adoption of this ASU to have a material impact on its consolidated financial statements except&#13;that there are significant additional reporting requirements under the new standard.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;In May 2016, the FASB issued ASU 2016-11, Revenue&#13;Recognition (Topic 605) and Derivatives and Hedging (Topic 815): Rescission of SEC Guidance Because of Accounting Standards Updates&#13;2014-09 and 2014-16 Pursuant to Staff Announcements at the March 3, 2016 EITF Meeting. This ASU rescinds SEC paragraphs pursuant&#13;to two SEC Staff Announcements at the March 3, 2016 Emerging Issues Task Force (EITF) meeting. Specifically, registrants should&#13;not rely on the following SEC Staff Observer comments upon adoption of Topic 606: (1) Revenue and Expense Recognition for Freight&#13;Services in Process, which is codified in paragraph 605-20-S99-2; (2) Accounting for Shipping and Handling Fees and Costs, which&#13;is codified in paragraph 605-45-S99-1; (3) Accounting for Consideration Given by a Vendor to a Customer (including Reseller of&#13;the Vendor&amp;#8217;s Products), which is codified in paragraph 605-50-S99-1; and (4) Accounting for Gas-Balancing Arrangements (i.e.,&#13;use of the &amp;#8220;entitlements method&amp;#8221;), which is codified in paragraph 932-10-S99-5. This ASU becomes effective upon adoption&#13;of ASU 2014-09, which is effective for fiscal years, and for interim periods within those fiscal years, beginning after December&#13;15, 2017. The Company has not yet begun to consider the alternatives of adoption of this ASU or its impact on its consolidated&#13;financial statements.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;In May 2016, the FASB issued ASU 2016-12, Revenue&#13;from Contracts with Customers (Topic 606): Narrow-Scope Improvements and Practical Expedients. This ASU does not change the core&#13;principle of the guidance in Topic 606. Instead, the amendments provide clarifying guidance in a few narrow areas and add some&#13;practical expedients to the guidance. This ASU has the same effective date as the new revenue standard, which is effective for&#13;fiscal years, and for interim periods within those fiscal years, beginning after December 15, 2017. The Company is currently evaluating&#13;the impact of the pending adoption of this new standard on its consolidated financial statements. The Company is considering the&#13;alternatives of adoption of this ASU. Currently, the Company does not expect the adoption of this ASU to have a material impact&#13;on its financial statements except that there are significant additional reporting requirements under the new standard.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;In August 2016, the FASB issued ASU 2016-15,&#13;Statement of Cash Flows (Topic 230): Classification of Certain Cash Receipts and Cash Payments. The new guidance is intended to&#13;reduce diversity in practice in how transactions are classified in the statement of cash flows. This ASU is effective for fiscal&#13;years, and for interim periods within those fiscal years, beginning after December 15, 2017. Early adoption is permitted. The Company&#13;is currently evaluating the impact of this ASU on its consolidated financial statements and currently the Company has determined&#13;there to be no impact of this ASU on its financial statements and related disclosures.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman

   &lt;td&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td&gt;&lt;font style=font-size: 8pt&gt;$&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=text-align: right&gt;&lt;font style=font-size: 8pt&gt;2.11&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&#13;&lt;tr&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=vertical-align: bottom; padding-left: 0.25in&gt;&lt;font style=font-size: 8pt&gt;Vested&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=vertical-align: bottom&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=vertical-align: bottom&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=vertical-align: bottom; text-align: right&gt;&lt;font style=font-size: 8pt&gt;(257,261&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=vertical-align: bottom&gt;&lt;font style=font-size: 8pt&gt;)&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=text-align: right&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;font style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;The Company accounts for share-based&#13;compensation to employees in accordance with ASC 718 &lt;i&gt;Compensation&amp;#8212;Stock Compensation. Share &lt;/i&gt;based compensation&#13;to employees is measured at the grant date, based on the fair value of the award, and is recognized as expense over the&#13;requisite employee service period. The Company accounts for share based compensation to other than employees in accordance&#13;with Financial Standards Accounting Board (FASB) ASC 505-50. Equity instruments issued to other than employees are valued at&#13;the earlier of a commitment date or upon completion of the services, based on the fair value of the equity instruments and is&#13;recognized as expense over the service period. The Company estimates the fair value of share based payments using the&#13;Black-Scholes option pricing model for common stock options and warrants and the latest fair market price of the&#13;Company&amp;#8217;s common stock for common share issuances. The Company has not experienced any forfeitures and does not expect&#13;forfeitures.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 8pt Times New Roman
 Times
